Jamison Brereton

22 (318)
Indra
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Within a slender frame depicting IndraтАЩs presence at and participation in our sac rifice is fitted a celebration of IndraтАЩs great deeds and, especially, his aggressiveness in performing them. The hymn begins (vs. 1) with a brief catalogue of the elements Indra wants at the ritual, which leads immediately to the praise of IndraтАЩs uncon trolled power, the terror he inspires in the cosmos, and the fortunate result of his greatest deed, the release of the waters following his defeat of Vr╠еtra (vss. 2тАУ7). Verse 8 marks a return to the ritual here-and-now, with a hope that our preparations will bring Indra to our sacrifice. Verses 9тАУ10 then list the various things we want Indra to do for us, marked by the heavy repetition of тАЬfor us/to usтАЭ at the beginning of every half-verse (a pattern actually begun in vs. 8c with тАЬtoward us,тАЭ and ending with an extra repetition in the final p─Бda 10d). The hymn ends with the V─Бmadeva Indra-cycle refrain (vs. 11).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra Hoffmann treats and translates the first four vss. of this hymn (Injunk. 186- 88) as an ex. of тАЬdie erw├дhnende Beschreibung eines pr├дteritalen TatbestandesтАЭ associated with the general description of a god. He notes the unclear boundaries between past and present in such contexts.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSince the great and mighty Indra is propitiated by our (oblations), since he desires (them) from us, may he, the possessor of opulence, who comes wielding the thunderbolt of his strength, accept the (sacrificial) food, the hymn, the Soma libation, and the prayers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Food, hymn, soma and prayhers: an allusion to the fourfold forms of offering worship, Brahm─Б, Stoma, Soma and Uktha: the first is the cakes steeped in butter– offerings or obaltions; the second, the praise that is recited aloud; the third, the libation of the Soma; and the fourth, the praise or prayer that is repeated silently or in a lower tone not chanted or sung].

Jamison Brereton

What of ours Indra enjoys and what he is eager for, that of ours will the great, explosive one arrange to be right here:
the sacred formulation, the praise song, the soma, and the recitationsтАФ he, the bounteous, who goes on bearing the stone with strength,

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. propounds a novel version of divine-human interaction: it suggests that what a god wants from us – the verbal and material offerings we make to him at the sacrifice – he actually arranges to have available there. There seems no other way to read the ─Б╠БтИЪkс╣Ы тАШmake (to be) here, bring hereтАЩ in b (тАж karat тАж ─Б╠Б). This model almost reduces the human role to being middlemen in a loop connecting the god with himself, in contrast to the usual reciprocal model in which each side (divine / human) makes its own contribution.

In d ├йti appears to be used as an auxiliary with the participle b├нbhrat (so also Hoffmann, with ref. to Delbr├╝ck, AiS 390), though Geldner seems to take it as a full lexical verb (тАЬтАж tragend ausziehtтАЭ). Engl. тАЬgoes on X-ingтАЭ captures both the literal sense and the auxiliary function of the verb here.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe showerer (of benefits), casting with his hands the quadrangular bolt that causes rain, fierce, the chief of leaders, the achiever of (glorious) acts, is desirous of the prosperity of the investing Paruс╣гс╣Зi (river), whose (bordering) districts he has frequented through regard.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The investing Paruс╣гс╣Зi: ┼лrс╣З─Бm paruс╣гс╣З─лm = acch─Бdik─Бm parvavat─лm nad─лm, the river having joints or bends covering; whose bordering districts he has frequented: the text is, yasy─Бс╕е parv─Бс╣Зi sakhy─Бya vivye = liс╣н, those joints through friendship he has approached; the explanation: yasy─Бс╕е nadhyaс╕е bhinn─Бn de┼Ы─Бn sakhikarmaс╣Зe saс╣Гvс╣Ыtav─Бn, the separate districts of which river he has, for the sake of friendly acts,covered or concealed

Jamison Brereton

The bull, hurling with his arms the four-edged (weapon), which is the repository of bullish strengthтАФthe powerful, most manly, able one,
clothing himself in Paruс╣гс╣З─л River [/gray] wool [=foam] for beautyтАФ(the Paruс╣гс╣З─л River) in whose tufts he has wrapped himself for partnership (with the Maruts).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гandhi- has been variously explained. Oldenberg rejects the reading as тАЬsinnlosтАЭ and suggests an emendation to *tr├нс╣гandhi-, remarking that the vajra is so described in AV XI.10.3, 27. The influence of preceding vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б would account for the change. Hoffmann (MSS 8 [1956]: 15 = Aufs. II.395-96) instead suggests it is a haplology of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa-saс╣Гdhi- тАШmit starker VerbindungтАЩ, which in his view describes the binding of the head of the vajra, which he thinks was a hammer-like weapon, to the shaft. One of the unexamined assumptions of both OldenbergтАЩs and HoffmannтАЩs interpretations is that the weapon referred to here is the vajra and that this is identical to the stone (├б┼Ыman-) in 1d. As I argue ad I.152.2 (see comm. thereon), there is no reason to assume here that the stone = vajra or that the unnamed weapon in 2a is identical to both. A form of v├бjra- is found in 3c, but it need not be the same as the weapon(s) referred to in 1d and 2a – and in fact there is some reason to believe it is not, as the weapon here is being тАШhurledтАЩ (├бsyan), and to my knowledge the vajra is never thrown while stones regularly are (e.g., I.172.2). In my opinion the weapon in 2a is the stone of 1d and the qualifier vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гandhi- is a formation like iс╣гu-dh├н- тАШrepository of arrows, quiverтАЩ, uda-dh├н- тАШrepository of water, spring, basinтАЩ, utsa-dh├н- тАШfountainheadтАЩ тАФ hence тАШrepository of bullish(ness)тАЩ. The difference in accent can be attributed to the influence of immediately preceding vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б. The combining form vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan-, rather than more common vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa-, is also found in vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зvant- and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣З-vasu-.

The anomalous med. them. participle uс╣г├бm─Бna- тАШclothing oneselfтАЩ, as if to an otherwise unattested 6th cl. pres. to тИЪvas тАШwearтАЩ, belongs with the other unexpected med. participles (both them. and athem.) to тИЪva┼Ы тАШbe eagerтАЩ and тИЪvas тАШwearтАЩ found in this Indra cycle. See disc. ad IV.16.14 and IV.19.4 and cf. u┼Ы─Бn├б- in the next hymn (IV.23.1).

The second hemistich is best interpreted in the context of V.52.9, a Marut hymn, where the Maruts p├бruс╣гс╣Зy─Бm, ┼л╠Бrс╣З─Б vasata тАЬclothe themselves in the wool [=foam] in the Paruс╣гс╣З─л (River).тАЭ Note that in that passage p├бruс╣гс╣Зy─Бm and ┼л╠Бrс╣З─Б are in different cases and numbers (fem. loc. sg. and fem. acc. pl. respectively) unlike here, where both are fem. acc. sg. Their grammatical difference in V.52.9, which imposes a semantic separation, makes it less likely here that p├бruс╣гс╣З─лm is simply an adj.

modifying ┼л╠Бrс╣З─Бm, as Hoffmann (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it: тАЬin shaggy woolтАЭ (Hoffmann: тАЬin zottige (?) WolleтАЭ; Witzel Got┼Н тАЬin struppige WolleтАЭ). Since p├бruс╣гс╣З─л- is simply the fem. to paruс╣г├б-, which is otherwise a color term (тАШgrayтАЩ), the introduction of тАШshaggyтАЩ would also be puzzling. I therefore essentially follow GeldnerтАЩs interpr. He takes p├бruс╣гс╣З─лm тАж ┼л╠Бrс╣З─Бm as an unmarked simile: тАЬin the Paruс╣гс╣З─л (River) (like) woolтАЭ; I take it rather as a metaphor: тАЬin the Paruс╣гс╣З─л тАШwoolтАЩ [=foam].тАЭ The color gray enters this image in two ways. On the one hand, itтАЩs quite possible that the Paruс╣гс╣З─л River was so called because it appeared gray; on the other, river foam in general is gray-ish (and tufty, like wool), as google images of river foam show (unfortunately mostly of polluted rivers).

The unexpressed connection with the Maruts via the passage just cited is also expressed in p─Бda d through sakhy─Б╠Бya тАШfor partnershipтАЩ, where the partners must be the Maruts.

The word p├бrvan- usually refers to a joint or segment; with Geldner, I take it in this image to refer to tufts or articulated hunks of foam, like tufts of wool. With Geldner I also think thereтАЩs a secondary word association between p├бruс╣гс╣З─л- and p├бrvan- (/ p├бru(с╣г)-).

Griffith

Bull, hurler of the four-edged rain-producer with both his arms, strong, mighty, most heroic;
Wearing as wool Parusni for adornment, whose joints for sake of friendship he hath covered.

Geldner

Der Bullenhafte, der die einen Bullen enthaltende vierkantige Keule mit den Armen schleudert, der Gewaltige, Mannhafteste, M├дchtige, der zum Prunk sich in die Parusni wie Wolle kleidet, deren Flocken er zur Freundschaft umgelegt hat:

Grassmann

Der starke Held, den vierfachschneid’gen Blitzstrahl mit beiden Armen schleudernd, kr├дftig, mannhaft, Zum Schmuck sich kleidend in die flock’ge Wolle, aufsparend ihre Flocken f├╝r die Freunde.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho diine, most divine, as soon as born (was endowed) with abundant viands, and great energies, holding in his arms the willing thunderbolt, and causing by his strength (both) heaven and earth to tremble.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The god who, being born as the best of gods, is great by reason of his prizes and his great explosive powers,
having taken the eager mace in his arms, he makes heaven tremble by his onslaught, as well as earth,

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation I take the whole vs. as a single sentence, with ab a relative clause to the main cl. in cd. Geldner (Hoffmann/Witzel Got┼Н) take b as the main clause to the rel.

cl. in a and take cd separately. This is entirely possible; there is no grammatical marking to determine the structure, since b lacks a finite verb. Since b is a repeated p─Бda (VI.32.4b), it might indeed be better to take it as an independent unit and follow the Geldner interpr.

The distraction of #dy─Б╠Бm … bh┼л╠Бma# in d is paralleled by 4b #dya├║r … kс╣г─Б╠Бс╕е#.

Griffith

God who of all the Gods was born divinest, endowed with ample strength and mighty powers,
And bearing in his arrns the yearning thunder, with violent rush caused heaven and earth to tremble.

Geldner

Der Gott, der als der erste Gott geboren gro├Я an Siegen und an gro├Яen Kr├дften ist, er macht Himmel und Erde durch sein Ungest├╝m erbeben, wenn er die begierige Keule in den Armen h├дlt.

Grassmann

Der kaum geboren, schon der st├дrkste Gott war, an raschem Muthe gross und grossen Kr├дften, Den will’gen Blitz in seine Arme nehmend, macht beben er durch Andrang Erd’ und Himmel.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAll the high plural ces, and the many low paces, the heaven and the earth, trembled (through fear) of the mighty (Indra) at his birth; the strong (Indra) cherishes the parents of the moving (Sun), and the winds, like men, make a noise in their peregrination.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Parents of the moving sun: m─Бtar─Б bharati goс╕е: goс╕е = gantuс╕е s┼лryasya

Jamison Brereton

(And) all the (river)banks and the many (river)bedsтАФ(and) heaven trembles, and the earth, before the towering one at his birth.
The explosive one brings the two mothers here [=Heaven and Earth?], (brings) here (the milk? [=rain?]) of the cow. The winds in their
circling roar constantly like men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, polarized #dya├║r … kс╣г─Б╠Бс╕е# in b match the same (conceptual) pair in the same positions in 3d. Here in 4b the disjunction is emphasized by the fact that the two nominatives are subjects of a singular verb (rejata). The connection of the 3d and 4b is signaled by the fact that the same root provides the verb in both 3d and 4b: trans.-cause. rejayat and intrans. rejata respectively (both injunctives), and heaven and earth switch grammatical identity and function from object to subject.

P─Бda a sits somewhat uncomfortably between these two complementary p─Бdas.

The river banks and beds seem rather paltry natural features next to heaven and earth, which flank them. But they may serve a grammatical purpose: both NPs (v├н┼Ыv─Б r├│dh─Бс╣Гsi [neut. pl.] and prav├бtaс╕е тАж p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е [fem. pl.]) are neutral as to case (nom. vs. acc.) and can thus serve as a pivot, available as both acc. objects for rejayat in 3d and nom. subjects for rejata in 4b. (Of course, although the neuter pl. could be the subject of a sg. verb, technically speaking a feminine pl. should not, but this does not seem a problem to me, as the neut. pl. leads the conjoined NP and would set the syntactic tone – and they are pretty distant from the verb anyway.) P─Бda c produces problems on several fronts. Who are the mother and father (m─Бt├бr─Б)? (Oldenberg flatly announces he has no intention of trying to find out.) Why is the verb (bh├бrati) accented? Why are there two instances of ─Б╠Б? What is the cow (g├│с╕е) doing grammatically and/or conceptually? The only word that is not problematic (though see below) is ┼Ыuс╣гm─л╠Б, which must refer to Indra, as in 1b. I do not have entirely satisfactory answers to the puzzles. Probably the default referent for m─Бt├бr─Б would be Heaven and Earth, and they have figured prominently just previously. But there is the problem that Heaven and Earth are not particularly mobile, so how is it that Indra тАЬbrings them hereтАЭ? As for the accent on bh├бrati, Geldner suggests that p─Бda c is dependent on either ab or c, without overt subordination. Oldenberg (ZDMG 60 [1906]: 725-26 = KlSch 200-201) places it in the class of тАЬpriorischer NebensatzтАЭ (to the main cl. in p─Бda d), but c doesnтАЩt seem to provide sufficient grounding for d to justify the verbal accent.

Hoffmann (Injunk. 187 n. 147) cites OldenbergтАЩs own citation of himself (given above), but also what is the more likely explanation, given by Oldenberg in the same art. (708-12, esp.

711 = KlSch. 186): that it is implicitly antithetical, participating in two interlocked constructions, what Oldenberg (711 = 186) designates pavp╬▒ (that is, PREV [x-word] VERB PREV [corresponding x-╠Бword]) – with, in our passage, ─Б╠Бas the PREV, m─Б╠Бt├бr─Б тАж g├│с╕е as x and x,╠Б and bh├бrati as accented VERB. In his exx. nothing intervenes between VERB and the repeated PREV, unlike ┼Ыuс╣гm─л╠Бhere, but I consider this a minor variant in the model. Perhaps more problematic is that m─Бt├бr─Б and g├│с╕е do not correspond grammatically, but again I would prefer to work with a more flexible model (and see below). In this model the accent on the verb and the doubled ─Б╠Бfit under the same explanatory rubric, a desirable situation, all things being equal. (Such an explanation is blocked for Geldner, who thinks the two ─Б╠БтАЩs have different functions, the first preverb, the second preposition.) But what about the cow? One might note that thereтАЩs a similarly p─Бda-final g├│с╕е in 8d as well as another quite baffling one in the next hymn, IV.23.6. I also wonder if this pile-up of p─Бda-final g├│с╕е is not a sly reference to the impenetrable p─Бda-final g├│he in the previous hymn (IV.21.6b, 7c, 8c), which caused so many interpretational difficulties there (though they are not etymologically related, at least by our current understanding of g├│he). But this doesnтАЩt help us at all with the meaning or the function of g├│с╕е here. The first thing to consider is what case it is – gen. or abl. Geldner opts for the latter: Indra brings the two mothers from the cow (тАЬvon dem RindeтАЭ), though in n. 4c he also entertains the possibility of an ellipsis of a nominative with a dependent genitive g├│с╕е, тАЬ(son) of the cow,тАЭ namely the bull Indra.

As far as I can tell, Witzel Got┼Н also take it as an abl., but construed with ─Б╠Бin the sense of тАЬall the way toтАЭ (a marginal, but certainly attested, construction in the RV). There is nothing impossible about either of these interpr., but I do not see what they would mean in context, and neither Geldner nor Witzel Got┼Н give much help in that regard. For me the most appealing attempt to wring sense from this is HoffmannтАЩs (Injunk. 187). As in GeldnerтАЩs alternative, Hoffmann takes g├│с╕е as a gen. in an elliptical expression, but with the gapped item a second object to bh├бrati: тАЬHerbei bringt der Kraftschnaubende (seine) Eltern, herbei (das) der Kuh.тАЭ This makes good sense of the structure of the p─Бda (fitting better with OldenbergтАЩs pavp╬▒ scheme, since ╬▒ would now be grammatically parallel to a). So what is the тАЬdasтАЭ in HoffmannтАЩs tr.? He suggests тАШmilkтАЩ or similar, though not with a great deal of conviction. The published translation supplies тАШmilkтАЩ as a possible metaphor for тАШrainтАЩ, and given the roaring winds of p─Бda d, I think rain is quite likely the gapped object, since тАШcowтАЩ can be used of rain-bearing clouds. It also now occurs to me that it might instead be the Maruts (тАЬ[those] of the cowтАЭ), since they are the sons of the cow Pс╣Ы┼Ыni, as noted, e.g., in V.52.16, the same hymn that has the Paruс╣гс╣З─л River foam passage cited above (vs. 2). The Maruts would also fit with the violent roaring of the wind in d.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOf you, Indra, who are mighty, great are deeds, and to be proclaimed at all sacrifices, inasmuch as, high-minded hero, you, sustaining (the world), have by your strength slain Ahi with the resistless thunderbolt.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These great (deeds) of you, the great one, o Indra, are to be proclaimed at all the pressings:
that, o daring champion, having dared with daring, you worked over the serpent with your mace and strength. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. summarizing IndraтАЩs great deeds begin identically: t─Б╠Бt┼л╠Бte [ta in sandhi before vowel in 6]. The vss. appear at the exact center of the hymn and thus may count as an omphalos. Although both p─Бdas have IndraтАЩs deeds as subject, neither has a word for тАШdeedтАЩ.

Griffith

These are thy great deeds, Indra, thine, the Mighty, deeds to be told aloud at all libations,
That thou, O Hero, bold and boldly daring, didst with thy bolt, by strength, destroy the Dragon.

Geldner

Dies aber sind deine gro├Яen Taten des Gro├Яen, o Indra, die bei allen Somaopfern zu verk├╝nden sind, da├Я du, mutiger Held, mit wagemutigen Sinn es wagend den Drachen mit der Keule kr├дftig abgetan hast.

Grassmann

Dies grosse, was du grosser Indra wirktest, ist hoch zu r├╝hmen recht bei allen Opfern; Als, k├╝hner Held, mit K├╝hnheit k├╝hnlich strebend, die Schlange kr├дftig mit dem Blitz du schlugest.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMost powerful Indra, all these, your exploits, are verily true: (through fear of you), the showerer (of benefits), the cows shed (milk) from their udders; then, benevolent-minded (Indra), the rivers, fearing you, flow with rapidity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These (deeds) of yours all come true, o powerfully manly one: the cows stream forth from the udder of a bull;
then, being afraid of you, o you of bullish mind, the rivers charge forth at speed.594 IV.23

Jamison Brereton Notes

The b p─Бda contains one of the RVтАЩs beloved gender-bending paradoxes, with the cows coming out тАЬfrom the udder of a bullтАЭ (vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зa ┼л╠Бdhnaс╕е). Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) interprets this as rainwater coming from the sky (Parjanya or Heaven). I think it more likely that it concerns the Vala myth. IndraтАЩs other signature deed, the slaying of Vс╣Ыtra, was treated in the immediately preceding, paired verse (5d), and so we might expect mention of his other most prominent feat. In that case the тАЬbullтАЭ would be the Vala cave. On the other hand, this might continue the treatment of the Vс╣Ыtra myth in 5d (as Geldner also suggests, n. 6b), in which case the тАЬbullтАЭ would be Vс╣Ыtra himself or the mountain in which the waters were confined. The more thorough treatment of the waters in the Vс╣Ыtra myth in the following vs. 7 might support this latter view.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. summarizing IndraтАЩs great deeds begin identically: t─Б╠Бt┼л╠Бte [ta in sandhi before vowel in 6]. The vss. appear at the exact center of the hymn and thus may count as an omphalos. Although both p─Бdas have IndraтАЩs deeds as subject, neither has a word for тАШdeedтАЩ.

Another responsion: 6c ├бdh─Б ha / 7a ├бtr─Б╠Бha. Later in the p─Бda 7a t─Б╠Бu recalls the openings of 5a and 6a t─Б╠Бt┼л╠Б.

Griffith

True are all these thy deeds, O Most Heroic. The Milch-kine issued from the streaming udder.
In fear of thee, O thou of manly spirit, the rivers swiftly set themselves in motion.

Geldner

Dies aber sind alles wahre Taten von dir, du Mannhaftester: Die Milchk├╝he laufen aus dem Euter des Bullen hervor. Aus Furcht vor dir liefen die Str├╢me rasch davon, du Bullenmutiger.

Grassmann

Dies sind, sehr starker, alles deine Thaten, Milchtr├дnke rannen aus des Stieres Euter; Vor dir sich f├╝rchtend, der du Stieres Muth hast, bewegten da die Str├╢me sich in Eile.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдмрджреНрдмрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡реГрддреНрд░реЗрдг рдмрдзреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реАрдордиреБ рдПрддрд╛: рдирджреАрд░реБрджреНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдп рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдореН рдЕрддреНрдпрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рддрд┐рдВ рдмрдиреНрдзрдирдореН рдЕрдиреБ рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрджрдпрдзреНрдпреИ рдпрдерд╛рдХрд╛рдордВ рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рддреБрдВ рдкреНрд░ рдореБрдЪрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рдореЛрдЪрдпрдГ ред рд╣реЗ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╣ рдЕрддреНрд░реИрд╡ рдореЛрдЪрдирд╡реЗрд▓рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рддрд╛ рдЙ рддрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛ рдПрд╡ рджреЗрд╡реАрдГ рджреЗрд╡реНрдпреЛ рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕рд╛рд░рдГ рдирджреНрдпрдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реГрд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рдирджреАрд╡рд╛рдЪреА ред рдЕрд╡реЛрднрд┐рдГ рддреНрд╡рддреНрдХреГрддреИ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреИрдГ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддрд╡рдиреНрдд рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдирджреАрдкреВрд░рдгрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рдГ рдЬрдирд╛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThen, Indra, lord of horses, the divine sister (rivers) praise (you) for your protection when you did set them free to flow, after having been impeded (by Vс╣Ыtra) through a long confinement.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Right now, o Indra, master of the fallow bays, with your help these goddesses, the sisters, are praised,
when you let loose those (waters) that had been hard pressed, to let
them flow along their long trajectory.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most tr. take stavanta as passive, and this seems the correct interpr. The sisters are likely the rivers or waters released after the killing of Vс╣Ыtra. The question is why they would be praised as well as Indra. GeldnerтАЩs suggestion (n. 7ab) is that it is essentially a spill-over effect (not that he uses that term), that IndraтАЩs praiseworthy deed that brought the waters release also brought them praise by association.

I donтАЩt understand the double ├бnu (p─Бdas c and d), though my surmise is that the first one simply anticipates the second, which is in a semi-fixed expression d─лrgh─Б╠Бm ├бnu pr├бsitim (cf. X.40.10). Grassmann takes it as part of a preverb complex with тИЪmuc: ├бnu pr├б тИЪmuc тАШnacheinander loslassenтАЩ, and its position might support that assumption. But surely one of points in the Vс╣Ыtra myth is that the rivers burst out dramatically all at once. Geldner, by contrast, compares the identical sequence y├бt s─лm ├бnu in I.37.9, I.141.9, but those two passages seem unconnected with ours, with the ├бnu construed with preceding s─лm тАЬfollowing them.тАЭ (One can also compare IV.38.3 y├бс╣Г s─лm ├бnu, but this has yet a different sense.)

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe exhilarating Soma juice has been expressed; now may the curren flow to you, and may the expiatory power of the illustrious utterer of praise be directed towards us, as the quick rider holds firmly the reins of the steed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъam─л ┼Ыa┼Ыam─Бnasya ┼Ыaktiс╕е = ┼Ыamanam stuvataс╕е stuti karma; ┼Ыasa‘c─Бnasya = d─лptam─Бnasya

Jamison Brereton

The (soma-)plant has been squeezed out like an exhilarating river. By the labor of the laboring (priest), might the skill
of bright blazing (Agni) pull you here toward us, as a swift (horse pulls on) the powerfully strong reins of the cow [=leather?].

Jamison Brereton Notes

asmadry├аk opening 8c ushers in the suite of p─Бda-initial emphatic forms of the 1st pl. pronoun that lasts and intensifies through the real end of the hymn, vs. 10 (vs. 11 being the V─Бmadeva Indra refrain): 8c: asmadry├аk, 9a asm├й, 9c asm├бbhyam, 10a asm─Б╠Бkam, 10b asm├бbhyam, 10c asm├бbhyam, 10d asm─Б╠Бkam. K├╝mmel (310) interpr. pip─лс╕╖├й as presential, but there is in fact no way to tell: this is not only the only perfect form to this root attested anywhere but the only verb form to it in the RV (p─лс╕Нayati is added in the AV). I think it works better as an immediate past, although there is in practice little difference between my тАЬhas been squeezedтАЭ and K├╝mmelтАЩs тАЬausgepresst ist.тАЭ Geldner, flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa., takes m├бdyaс╕е with ─Бс╣Г┼Ы├║с╕е and explains the position of n├б as тАЬwie oft in P─Бdaausgang vor dem Vergleich.тАЭ But there seems no reason to ignore the usual structure of the simile, since m├бdyaс╕е easily modifies s├нndhuс╕е.

The syntax of bc is somewhat unusual, in that the subject / verb construction is split over the hemistich boundary (b тАж ┼Ыakt├нс╕е# c тАж yamy─Бс╕е#), while the object tv─Б is in WackernagelтАЩs position in p─Бda b. Moreover, at least in the published translation the genitive that limits the subj. ┼Ыakt├нс╕е is only found in the next p─Бda: ┼Ыu┼Ыuc─Бn├бsya. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take the gen. ┼Ыa┼Ыam─Бn├бsya in b as dependent on ┼Ыakt├нс╕е, with ┼Ы├бm─л an instr. adjunct to that participle: тАЬthe skill of the one laboring with laborтАЭ – in contrast to the published translation, where ┼Ыa┼Ыam─Бn├бsya is dependent on ┼Ы├бm─л. I now think that the Geldner interpr. may be preferable and would emend the published translation to тАЬMight the skill of the one laboring with labor (and) of the bright-blazing one pull тАжтАЭ The question is whether the two genitives are coreferential, with bright-blazing Agni identified as the one laboring with labor, or whether a (human) priest and Agni are both referred to. I do not think this can be determined, esp. since subjects of тИЪ┼Ыam elsewhere include both Agni and mortals.

The simile in d and the frame in bc have slightly different senses. In the simile the swift horse is pulling on the reins: it is so eager to reach its goal that it strains against the reins rather than being guided by them. In the frame the ┼Ыakt├нс╕е of the priest/god is strong enough to pull Indra to us. The difference in the relation of the accusative to the verb results from exploiting different senses of the root тИЪyam.

Despite OldenbergтАЩs expressed disbelief, I think Grassmann and Ludwig are correct in taking g├│с╕е тАШof the cowтАЩ to refer to reins made of leather. On p─Бda-final g├│h see also disc. ad vs. 4c.

Griffith

Pressed is the gladdening stalk as ’twere a river: so let the rite, the toiler’s power, attract thee
To us-ward, of the Bright One, as the courser strains his. exceedingly strong leather bridle.

Geldner

Der berauschende Stengel ist ausgedr├╝ckt wie ein Strom. Dich soll die Macht des mit Flei├Я den Opferdienst besorgenden, des Ergl├╝henden zu uns heranziehen wie das schnelle Ro├Я den Z├╝gel des Rindes, dich den Starkkr├дftigen.

Grassmann

Gepresst ward Soma wie ein Strom, der Rausch bringt, dich ziehe her der Dienst des eifrig th├дt’gen, Des gl├дnzenden zu uns her, wie ein Renner den sehr gewalt’gen Strang des Lederriemens.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬEnduring Indra, bestow upon us energies, excellent, superior, powerful; bring under subjection to us enemies deserving of death; demolish the weapon of the malevolent man.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For us activate your highest, most distinguished manly strengths and powers altogether, o overpowering one.
For us weaken obstacles to become easily smashed: smash the deadly weapon of the rapacious mortal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬHear our praises, Indra, and bestow upon us many kinds of food; fulfil all our desires, and know yourself, Maghavan, to be to us the donor of cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To us listen well, Indra; to us mete out glittering prizes.
To us you impel all plentiful gifts. For us become a giver of cows, o
bounteous one.

Griffith

Graciously listen to our prayer, O Indra, and strength of varied sort bestow thou on us.
Send to us all intelligence arid wisdom O Maghavan, be he who gives us cattle.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реИрдЛрд╖рд┐рдмрд┐рд╣реНрдГ рд╕рдореНрд╕реНрддреБрддреЛ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдорд┐рд╖рдордиреНрдирдВ рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗ рдорд╣реНрдпрдВ рдирджреНрдпреЛ рдирд╛рджреНрднрд┐рд░реНрдирджреАрд░рд┐рд╡ рдкрд┐рдкреЗрдГ ред рдкреНрдпрд╛рдпрдп ред рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдВ рдХреБрд░реБ ред рд╣реЗ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡реЛ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╕рдЮреНрдЬреНрдЮрдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡реЛрдкреЗрддреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рдирд╡реНрдпрдВ рдирд╡рддрд░рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдордХрд╛рд░рд┐ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ ред рд░рдереНрдпреЛ рд░рдерд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реВрдкрдпрд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рднрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рджрд░реНрдердВ рд╣рд╡реАрд░реВрдкрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░реЛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо ред рднреВрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдо рее резрез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorified (in the past), glorified, Indra, at present, satisfy your worshipper with food, as rivers (are filled with water); lord of horses, a new hymn has been made for you; may we, possessed of chariots, be ever diligent in (your) praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАУ Now praised, o Indra, now being sung, make refreshment swell for the singer like rivers.
A new sacred formulation has been made for you, o you of the fallow bays. Through our insightful thought may we be charioteers who
always win.

Griffith

Now, Indra! lauded, glorified with praises, let wealth swell hiah like rivers to the singer.
For thee a new hymn, Lord of Bays, is fashioned. May we, car-borne, through song be victors ever.

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░:
  • рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡реЛ рдЧреМрддрдордГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдФрд░ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд ! рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдЖрдк (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рд╣реБрдП (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрди рдХреЛ рджреЗрдХрд░ (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) рдирджрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рджреГрд╢ (рдиреБ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд░рд╛рдУ рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдиреБ) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рдЧрдпреЗ рдФрд░ (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдирд╡реАрди-рдирд╡реАрди (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдзрди рджрд┐рдпрд╛ рдЬрд╛рдп рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рд░рдердпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) рджрд╛рд╕реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╣рд┐рдд рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рд╕рдм рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрддреЗ рд╣реЛ, рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдорд┐рддреНрд░рддрд╛ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдмрд╣реБрдд рдзрди рдФрд░ рдЕрдиреНрди рджреЗрдХрд░ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░, рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА, рдзрд╛рд░рдг, рднреНрд░рдордг, рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН, рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдФрд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрезрее рдпрд╣ рдмрд╛рдЗрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЖрдард╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рдпрддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд╕реНрд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░ рдЗрд╖рдВ рджрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдирджреНрдпреЛ рди рдиреБ рдкреАрдкреЗрдГред рдпрддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдорд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдЧреГрдгрд╛рдиреЛ рдиреНрд╡рдХрд╛рд░рд┐ рддреЗ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рдирд╡реНрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рджреАрдпреЗрдд рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреН рд░рдереНрдпрдГ рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рддрд╡ рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреБ) (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдпрдЬреНрдЮреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдиреБ) (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реЗ (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) рд╕рд░рд┐рддрдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) рд╡рд░реНрдзрдп (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) (рддреЗ) (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдзрдирдореН (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдирд╡реАрдирдВ рдирд╡реАрдирдореН (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрджрд╛рд╕рд┐ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рд╕рд╣ рдореИрддреНрд░реАрдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рдкреБрд╖реНрдХрд▓рдзрдирдордиреНрдирдЮреНрдЪ рджрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рддрддрдВ рд╕рддреНрдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдо реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдзрд╛рд░рдгрднреНрд░рдордгрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрезрее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╖реНрдЯрдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛! рдЬреНрдпрд╛рд╡реЗрд│реА рддреВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрддреЛрд╕ рддреНрдпрд╛рд╡реЗрд│реА рддреБрдЭреНрдпрд╛рдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рдореИрддреНрд░реА рдХрд░реВрди рддреБрд▓рд╛ рдкреБрд╖реНрдХрд│ рдзрди рд╡ рдЕрдиреНрди рджреЗрдКрди рддреБрдЭрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЗрд▓рд╛ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее резрез рее
